&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Henry Rollins&lt;/b&gt; (born &lt;b&gt;Henry Lawrence Garfield&lt;/b&gt;; February 13, 1961) is an American musician, writer, journalist, publisher, actor, television and radio host, spoken word artist, comedian, and activist.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-laweekly_1-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-laweekly-1"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;1&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-2"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;2&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-3"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;3&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins hosts a weekly radio show on &lt;a href="/wiki/KCRW" title="KCRW"&gt;KCRW&lt;/a&gt;. He is also a regular columnist for &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly"&gt;LA Weekly&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_Australia" title="Rolling Stone Australia"&gt;Rolling Stone Australia&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-4"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;4&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After performing for the short-lived Washington D.C.-based band &lt;a href="/wiki/State_of_Alert" title="State of Alert"&gt;State of Alert&lt;/a&gt; in 1980, Rollins fronted the California &lt;a href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk" title="Hardcore punk"&gt;hardcore punk&lt;/a&gt; band &lt;a href="/wiki/Black_Flag_(band)" title="Black Flag (band)"&gt;Black Flag&lt;/a&gt; from August 1981 until mid-1986. Following the band's breakup, Rollins established the &lt;a href="/wiki/Independent_record_label" title="Independent record label"&gt;record label&lt;/a&gt; and publishing company &lt;a href="/wiki/2.13.61" title="2.13.61"&gt;2.13.61&lt;/a&gt; to release his spoken word albums, as well as forming the &lt;a href="/wiki/Rollins_Band" title="Rollins Band"&gt;Rollins Band&lt;/a&gt;, which toured with a number of lineups from 1987 until 2003, and during 2006.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Since Black Flag disbanded, Rollins has hosted numerous radio shows, such as &lt;i&gt;Harmony in My Head&lt;/i&gt; on &lt;a href="/wiki/Indie_103" title="Indie 103" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Indie 103&lt;/a&gt;, and television shows such as &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Henry_Rollins_Show" title="The Henry Rollins Show"&gt;The Henry Rollins Show&lt;/a&gt;,&lt;/i&gt; MTV's &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/120_Minutes" title="120 Minutes"&gt;120 Minutes&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, and &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Jackass_(TV_series)" title="Jackass (TV series)"&gt;Jackass&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;. He had recurring dramatic roles in the second season of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Anarchy" title="Sons of Anarchy"&gt;Sons of Anarchy&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, in the final seasons of the animated series &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Korra" title="The Legend of Korra"&gt;The Legend of Korra&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; as &lt;a href="/wiki/Zaheer_(The_Legend_of_Korra)" title="Zaheer (The Legend of Korra)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Zaheer&lt;/a&gt;, and has also had roles in several films. Rollins has also campaigned for various political causes in the United States, including promoting &lt;a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_States" title="LGBT rights in the United States"&gt;LGBT rights&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/World_Hunger_Relief" title="World Hunger Relief"&gt;World Hunger Relief&lt;/a&gt;, and an &lt;a href="/wiki/Peace_movement" title="Peace movement"&gt;end to war&lt;/a&gt; in particular.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As of 2013, Rollins is also the host of the educational history television series &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/10_Things_You_Don%27t_Know_About" title="10 Things You Don't Know About"&gt;10 Things You Don't Know About&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, joining the show for its second and third seasons. New episodes air weekly on &lt;a href="/wiki/H2_(TV_network)" title="H2 (TV network)"&gt;H2&lt;/a&gt; in the U.S.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24"&gt;&lt;a href="#With_Wartime"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;6.1.5&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;With Wartime&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"&gt;&lt;a href="#Spoken_word_2"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;6.2&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;Spoken word&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"&gt;&lt;a href="#Spoken_word_videos"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;6.3&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;Spoken word videos&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"&gt;&lt;a href="#Audio_books"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;6.4&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;Audio books&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"&gt;&lt;a href="#Guest_appearances_and_collaborations"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;6.5&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;Guest appearances and collaborations&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"&gt;&lt;a href="#Essays"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;6.6&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;Essays&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"&gt;&lt;a href="#References"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;7&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;References&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"&gt;&lt;a href="#Further_reading"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;Further reading&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"&gt;&lt;a href="#External_links"&gt;&lt;span class="tocnumber"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="toctext"&gt;External links&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life"&gt;Early life&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins was born Henry Lawrence Garfield in Washington, D.C, the only child of Iris and Paul Garfield.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-Biography_5-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-Biography-5"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-latimes_6-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-latimes-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;6&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-7"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;7&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-8"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;8&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; When he was three years old, his parents divorced and he was raised by his mother in &lt;a href="/wiki/Glover_Park" title="Glover Park"&gt;Glover Park&lt;/a&gt;, which was then an affluent neighborhood of Washington.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-Biography_5-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-Biography-5"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-9"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;9&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-10"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;10&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-ayad_11-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-ayad-11"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;11&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As a child and teenager, Rollins suffered from depression and low self-esteem.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a25_12-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a25-12"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;12&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In the fourth grade, he was diagnosed with &lt;a href="/wiki/Hyperactivity" title="Hyperactivity" class="mw-redirect"&gt;hyperactivity&lt;/a&gt; and took &lt;a href="/wiki/Methylphenidate" title="Methylphenidate"&gt;Ritalin&lt;/a&gt; for several years so that he could focus during school. He attended &lt;a href="/wiki/The_Bullis_School" title="The Bullis School" class="mw-redirect"&gt;The Bullis School&lt;/a&gt;, then an all-male preparatory school in &lt;a href="/wiki/Potomac,_Maryland" title="Potomac, Maryland"&gt;Potomac, Maryland&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-Biography_5-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-Biography-5"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;5&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;According to Rollins, the Bullis School helped him to develop a sense of discipline and a strong work ethic.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a25_12-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a25-12"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;12&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; It was at Bullis that he began writing.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-ayad_11-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-ayad-11"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;11&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 1987, Rollins said he had not seen his father since he was 18.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-latimes_6-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-latimes-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;6&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career"&gt;Music career&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Music career"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="State_of_Alert"&gt;State of Alert&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: State of Alert"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle"&gt;Main article: &lt;a href="/wiki/State_of_Alert" title="State of Alert"&gt;State of Alert&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After high school, Rollins attended &lt;a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University"&gt;American University&lt;/a&gt; in Washington D.C. for one semester, but dropped out in December 1979.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-latimes_6-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-latimes-6"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;6&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-13"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;13&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He began working minimum-wage jobs, including a job as a courier for kidney samples at the &lt;a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health"&gt;National Institutes of Health&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-popenter_14-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-popenter-14"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;14&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins developed an interest in &lt;a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock"&gt;punk rock&lt;/a&gt; after he and his friend &lt;a href="/wiki/Ian_MacKaye" title="Ian MacKaye"&gt;Ian MacKaye&lt;/a&gt; procured a copy of &lt;a href="/wiki/The_Ramones" title="The Ramones" class="mw-redirect"&gt;The Ramones&lt;/a&gt;'s eponymous &lt;a href="/wiki/Ramones_(album)" title="Ramones (album)"&gt;debut album&lt;/a&gt;; he later described it as a "akin to shooting heroin." From 1979 to 1980, Rollins was working as a roadie for Washington bands, including &lt;a href="/wiki/Teen_Idles" title="Teen Idles" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Teen Idles&lt;/a&gt;. When the band's singer Nathan Strejcek failed to appear for practice sessions, Rollins convinced the Teen Idles to let him sing. Word of Rollins's ability spread around the punk rock scene in Washington; &lt;a href="/wiki/Bad_Brains" title="Bad Brains"&gt;Bad Brains&lt;/a&gt; singer &lt;a href="/wiki/H.R." title="H.R."&gt;H.R.&lt;/a&gt; would sometimes get Rollins on stage to sing with him.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a26_15-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a26-15"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;15&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 1980, the Washington punk band The Extorts lost their frontman &lt;a href="/wiki/Lyle_Preslar" title="Lyle Preslar"&gt;Lyle Preslar&lt;/a&gt; to &lt;a href="/wiki/Minor_Threat" title="Minor Threat"&gt;Minor Threat&lt;/a&gt;. Rollins joined the rest of the band to form &lt;a href="/wiki/State_of_Alert" title="State of Alert"&gt;State of Alert&lt;/a&gt;, and became its frontman and vocalist. He put words to the band's five songs and wrote several more. S.O.A. recorded their sole EP, &lt;i&gt;No Policy&lt;/i&gt;, and released it in 1981 on MacKaye's &lt;a href="/wiki/Dischord_Records" title="Dischord Records"&gt;Dischord Records&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-16"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;16&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; S.O.A. disbanded after a total of a dozen concerts and one EP. Rollins had enjoyed being the band's frontman, and had earned a reputation for fighting in shows. He later said: "I was like nineteen and a young man all full of steam [...] &lt;i&gt;Loved&lt;/i&gt; to get in the dust-ups." By this time, Rollins had become the manager of the Georgetown &lt;a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4agen-Dazs" title="Hagen-Dazs"&gt;Hagen-Dazs&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream"&gt;ice cream&lt;/a&gt; store; his steady employment had helped to finance the S.O.A. EP.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a27_17-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a27-17"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;17&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Black_Flag"&gt;Black Flag&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Black Flag"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle"&gt;Main article: &lt;a href="/wiki/Black_Flag_(band)" title="Black Flag (band)"&gt;Black Flag (band)&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 1980, a friend gave Rollins and MacKaye a copy of &lt;a href="/wiki/Black_Flag_(band)" title="Black Flag (band)"&gt;Black Flag&lt;/a&gt;'s &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Nervous_Breakdown_(EP)" title="Nervous Breakdown (EP)"&gt;Nervous Breakdown&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; EP. Rollins soon became a fan of the band, exchanging letters with bassist &lt;a href="/wiki/Chuck_Dukowski" title="Chuck Dukowski"&gt;Chuck Dukowski&lt;/a&gt; and later inviting the band to stay in his parents' home when Black Flag toured the East Coast in December 1980.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-18"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;18&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; When Black Flag returned to the East Coast in 1981, Rollins attended as many of their concerts as he could. At an impromptu show in a New York bar, Black Flag's vocalist &lt;a href="/wiki/Dez_Cadena" title="Dez Cadena"&gt;Dez Cadena&lt;/a&gt; allowed Rollins to sing "Clocked In", a song Rollins had asked the band to play in light of the fact that he had to drive back to Washington, D.C. to begin work.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a28_19-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a28-19"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;19&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Unbeknownst to Rollins, Cadena wanted to switch to guitar, and the band was looking for a new vocalist.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a28_19-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a28-19"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;19&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The band was impressed with Rollins' singing and stage demeanor, and the next day, after a semi-formal audition at Tu Casa Studio in NYC, they asked him to become their permanent vocalist. Despite some doubts, he accepted, in part because of MacKaye's encouragement. His high level of energy and intense personality suited the band's style, but Rollins' diverse tastes in music were a key factor in his being selected as singer; Black Flag's founder &lt;a href="/wiki/Greg_Ginn" title="Greg Ginn"&gt;Greg Ginn&lt;/a&gt; was growing restless creatively and wanted a singer who was willing to move beyond simple, three-chord punk.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a29_20-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a29-20"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;20&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tright"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Black_Flag_logo.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Black_Flag_logo.jpg/200px-Black_Flag_logo.jpg" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Black_Flag_logo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Black_Flag_logo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="250" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Black_Flag_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
The band's logo was created by artist &lt;a href="/wiki/Raymond_Pettibon" title="Raymond Pettibon"&gt;Raymond Pettibon&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After joining Black Flag in 1981, Rollins quit his job at Hagen-Dazs, sold his car, and moved to Los Angeles. Upon arriving in Los Angeles, Rollins got the Black Flag logo &lt;a href="/wiki/Tattoo" title="Tattoo"&gt;tattooed&lt;/a&gt; on his left bicep&lt;sup id="cite_ref-popenter_14-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-popenter-14"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;14&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and chose the stage name of Rollins, a surname he and MacKaye had used as teenagers.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a29_20-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a29-20"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;20&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins played his first show with Black Flag on August 21, 1981 at Cuckoo's Nest in Costa Mesa, California.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-21"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;21&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins was in a different environment in Los Angeles; the police soon realized he was a member of Black Flag, and he was hassled as a result. Rollins later said: "That really scared me. It freaked me out that an adult would do that. [...] My little eyes were opened big time."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-22"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;22&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Before concerts, as the rest of the band tuned up, Rollins would stride about the stage dressed only in a pair of black shorts, grinding his teeth; to focus before the show, he would squeeze a pool ball.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-23"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;23&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; His stage persona impressed several critics; after a 1982 show in &lt;a href="/wiki/Anacortes,_Washington" title="Anacortes, Washington"&gt;Anacortes, Washington&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Sub Pop&lt;/i&gt; critic &lt;a href="/wiki/Calvin_Johnson_(musician)" title="Calvin Johnson (musician)"&gt;Calvin Johnson&lt;/a&gt; wrote: "Henry was incredible. Pacing back and forth, lunging, lurching, growling; it was all real, the most intense emotional experiences I have ever seen."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-24"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;24&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By 1983, Rollins' stage persona was increasingly alienating him from the rest of Black Flag. During a show in England, Rollins assaulted a member of the audience, who attacked Ginn; Ginn later scolded Rollins, calling him a "macho asshole".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-25"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;25&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; A legal dispute with &lt;a href="/wiki/Unicorn_Records" title="Unicorn Records" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Unicorn Records&lt;/a&gt; held up further Black Flag releases until 1984, and Ginn was slowing the band's tempo down so that they would remain innovative. In August 1983, guitarist &lt;a href="/wiki/Dez_Cadena" title="Dez Cadena"&gt;Dez Cadena&lt;/a&gt; had left the band; a stalemate lingered between Dukowski and Ginn, who wanted Dukowski to leave, before Ginn fired Dukowski outright.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-26"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;26&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; 1984's &lt;a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music"&gt;heavy metal music&lt;/a&gt;-influenced &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/My_War" title="My War"&gt;My War&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; featured Rollins screaming and wailing throughout many of the songs; the band's members also grew their hair to confuse the band's hardcore punk audience.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a47_27-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a47-27"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;27&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Black Flag's change in musical style and appearance alienated many of their original fans, who focused their displeasure on Rollins by punching him in the mouth, stabbing him with pens, or scratching him with their nails, among other methods. He often fought back, dragging audience members on stage and assaulting them. During a Black Flag concert, Rollins punched a fan repeatedly in the face that had continuously reached for his microphone. &lt;sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-28"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;28&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;Rollins became increasingly alienated from the audience; in his tour diary, Rollins wrote "When they spit at me, when they grab at me, they aren't hurting me. When I push out and mangle the flesh of another, it's falling so short of what I really want to do to them."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-29"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;29&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; During the Unicorn legal dispute, Rollins had started a weight-lifting program, and by their 1984 tours, he had become visibly well-built; journalist &lt;a href="/wiki/Michael_Azerrad" title="Michael Azerrad"&gt;Michael Azerrad&lt;/a&gt; later commented that "his powerful physique was a metaphor for the impregnable emotional shield he was developing around himself."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a47_27-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a47-27"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;27&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins has since replied that "no, the training was just basically a way to push myself."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-smhinterview_30-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-smhinterview-30"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;30&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Rollins_Band_and_solo_releases"&gt;Rollins Band and solo releases&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rollins Band and solo releases"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle"&gt;Main article: &lt;a href="/wiki/Rollins_Band" title="Rollins Band"&gt;Rollins Band&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tright"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg/300px-HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg" width="300" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg/450px-HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg/600px-HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3097" data-file-height="1900" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:HenryRollins_Performing_1993.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
Rollins performing with the &lt;a href="/wiki/Rollins_Band" title="Rollins Band"&gt;Rollins Band&lt;/a&gt; in 1993&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Before Black Flag disbanded in August 1986, Rollins had already toured as a solo spoken word artist.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-31"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;31&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He released two solo records in 1987, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Hot_Animal_Machine" title="Hot Animal Machine"&gt;Hot Animal Machine&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, a collaboration with guitarist &lt;a href="/wiki/Chris_Haskett" title="Chris Haskett"&gt;Chris Haskett&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Drive_by_Shooting" title="Drive by Shooting"&gt;Drive by Shooting&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, recorded as "Henrietta Collins and the Wifebeating Childhaters";&lt;sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-32"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;32&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins also released his second spoken word album, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Big_Ugly_Mouth" title="Big Ugly Mouth"&gt;Big Ugly Mouth&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; in the same year. Along with Haskett, Rollins soon added &lt;a href="/wiki/Andrew_Weiss_(guitarist)" title="Andrew Weiss (guitarist)"&gt;Andrew Weiss&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Sim_Cain" title="Sim Cain"&gt;Sim Cain&lt;/a&gt;, both former members of Ginn's side-project &lt;a href="/wiki/Gone_(band)" title="Gone (band)"&gt;Gone&lt;/a&gt;, and called the new group &lt;a href="/wiki/Rollins_Band" title="Rollins Band"&gt;Rollins Band&lt;/a&gt;. The band toured relentlessly,&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amgrollins_33-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amgrollins-33"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;33&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and their 1987 debut album, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Life_Time_(Rollins_Band_album)" title="Life Time (Rollins Band album)"&gt;Life Time&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, was quickly followed by the outtakes and live collection &lt;i&gt;Do It&lt;/i&gt;. The band continued to tour throughout 1988; 1989 marked the release of another Rollins Band album, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Hard_Volume" title="Hard Volume"&gt;Hard Volume&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amghenry_34-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amghenry-34"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;34&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Another live album, &lt;i&gt;Turned On&lt;/i&gt;, and another spoken word release, &lt;i&gt;Live at McCabe's&lt;/i&gt;, followed in 1990.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;1991 saw the Rollins Band sign a distribution deal with Imago Records and appear at the &lt;a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza"&gt;Lollapalooza&lt;/a&gt; festival; both improved the band's presence. However, in December 1991, Rollins and his best friend &lt;a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole_(roadie)" title="Joe Cole (roadie)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Joe Cole&lt;/a&gt; were accosted by two armed robbers outside Rollins's home. Cole was murdered by a gunshot to the head, Rollins escaped without injury but police initially suspected him in the murder and detained him for ten hours.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-35"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;35&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Although traumatized by Cole's death, as chronicled in his book &lt;i&gt;Now Watch Him Die&lt;/i&gt;, Rollins continued to release new material; the spoken-word album &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Human_Butt" title="Human Butt"&gt;Human Butt&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; appeared in 1992 on his own record label, &lt;a href="/wiki/2.13.61" title="2.13.61"&gt;2.13.61&lt;/a&gt;. The Rollins Band released &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_End_of_Silence" title="The End of Silence"&gt;The End of Silence&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, Rollins's first charting album.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amghenry_34-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amghenry-34"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;34&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The following year, Rollins released a spoken-word double album, &lt;i&gt;The Boxed Life&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-36"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;36&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The Rollins Band embarked upon the &lt;i&gt;End of Silence&lt;/i&gt; tour; bassist Weiss was fired towards its end and replaced by funk and jazz bassist &lt;a href="/wiki/Melvin_Gibbs" title="Melvin Gibbs"&gt;Melvin Gibbs&lt;/a&gt;. According to critic Steve Huey, 1994 was Rollins's "breakout year".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-amghenry_34-2" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-amghenry-34"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;34&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The Rollins Band appeared at &lt;a href="/wiki/Woodstock_94" title="Woodstock 94" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Woodstock 94&lt;/a&gt; and released &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Weight_(album)" title="Weight (album)"&gt;Weight&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, which ranked on the Billboard Top 40. Rollins released &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Get_in_the_Van" title="Get in the Van"&gt;Get in the Van: On the Road with Black Flag&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, a double-disc set of him reading from his Black Flag tour diary of the same name; he won the Grammy for &lt;a href="/wiki/Best_Spoken_Word_Recording" title="Best Spoken Word Recording" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Best Spoken Word Recording&lt;/a&gt; as a result. Rollins was named 1994's "Man of the Year" by the American men's magazine &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Details_(magazine)" title="Details (magazine)"&gt;Details&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and became a contributing columnist to the magazine. With the increased exposure, Rollins made several appearances on American music channels MTV and &lt;a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1"&gt;VH1&lt;/a&gt; around this time, and made his Hollywood film debut in 1994 in &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Chase_(1994_film)" title="The Chase (1994 film)"&gt;The Chase&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; playing a police officer.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-37"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;37&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 1995, the Rollins Band's record label, Imago Records, declared itself bankrupt. Rollins began focusing on his spoken word career. He released &lt;i&gt;Everything&lt;/i&gt;, a recording of a chapter of his book &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Eye_Scream" title="Eye Scream" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Eye Scream&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; with free jazz backing, in 1996. He continued to appear in various films, including &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Heat_(1995_film)" title="Heat (1995 film)"&gt;Heat&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Johnny_Mnemonic_(film)" title="Johnny Mnemonic (film)"&gt;Johnny Mnemonic&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Lost_Highway_(film)" title="Lost Highway (film)"&gt;Lost Highway&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;. The Rollins Band signed to &lt;a href="/wiki/Dreamworks_Records" title="Dreamworks Records" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Dreamworks Records&lt;/a&gt; in 1997 and soon released &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Come_in_and_Burn" title="Come in and Burn" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Come in and Burn&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, but it did not receive as much critical acclaim as their previous material. Rollins continued to release spoken-word book readings, releasing &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Black_Coffee_Blues" title="Black Coffee Blues"&gt;Black Coffee Blues&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; in the same year. In 1998, Rollins released &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Think_Tank_(Rollins)" title="Think Tank (Rollins)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Think Tank&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, his first set of non-book-related spoken material in five years.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By 1998, Rollins felt that the relationship with his backing band had run its course, and the line-up disbanded. He had produced a Los Angeles &lt;a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock"&gt;hard rock&lt;/a&gt; band called &lt;a href="/wiki/Mother_Superior_(band)" title="Mother Superior (band)"&gt;Mother Superior&lt;/a&gt;, and invited them to form a new incarnation of the Rollins Band. Their first album, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Get_Some_Go_Again" title="Get Some Go Again"&gt;Get Some Go Again&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, was released two years later. The Rollins Band released several more albums, including 2001's &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Nice_(Rollins_Band_album)" title="Nice (Rollins Band album)"&gt;Nice&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and 2003's &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Rise_Above:_24_Black_Flag_Songs_to_Benefit_the_West_Memphis_Three" title="Rise Above: 24 Black Flag Songs to Benefit the West Memphis Three"&gt;Rise Above: 24 Black Flag Songs to Benefit the West Memphis Three&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;. After 2003, the band became inactive as Rollins focused on radio and television work. During a 2006 appearance on &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Tom_Green%27s_House_Tonight" title="Tom Green's House Tonight"&gt;Tom Green Live!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, Rollins stated that he "may never do music again"&lt;sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-38"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;38&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; a feeling which he reiterated in 2011 when talking to &lt;i&gt;Trebuchet&lt;/i&gt; magazine.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-39"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;39&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In an &lt;a href="/wiki/Interview" title="Interview"&gt;interview&lt;/a&gt; with &lt;i&gt;Culture Brats&lt;/i&gt;, Henry admitted he had sworn off music for good  "... and I must say that I miss it every day. I just don't know honestly what I could do with it that's different."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-40"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;40&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2014, Rollins admitted a disdain for rehashing old music for the sake of it - "I dont want to play old music. To me, it is fighting battles that are already over and calling yourself a warrior. For me, I see no courage or adventure in doing the old thing over again. If others want to, thats for them. For myself, I have to move on. Life is too short to live in the past. There is a lot to be done."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-41"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;41&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style"&gt;Musical style&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Musical style"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As a vocalist, Rollins has adopted a number of styles through the years. Rollins was initially noted in the &lt;a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C._hardcore" title="Washington, D.C. hardcore"&gt;Washington, D.C. hardcore&lt;/a&gt; scene for what journalist &lt;a href="/wiki/Michael_Azerrad" title="Michael Azerrad"&gt;Michael Azerrad&lt;/a&gt; described as a "compelling, raspy howl."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a26_15-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a26-15"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;15&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; With State of Alert, Rollins "spat out the lyrics like a bellicose auctioneer."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a27_17-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a27-17"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;17&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He adopted a similar style after joining Black Flag in 1981. By their album &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Damaged_(Black_Flag_album)" title="Damaged (Black Flag album)"&gt;Damaged&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, however, Black Flag began to incorporate a &lt;a href="/wiki/Swung_note" title="Swung note" class="mw-redirect"&gt;swing beat&lt;/a&gt; into their style. Rollins then abandoned his &lt;a href="/wiki/State_of_Alert" title="State of Alert"&gt;S.O.A.&lt;/a&gt; "bark" and adopted the band's swing.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-a32_42-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-a32-42"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;42&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins later explained: "What I was doing kind of matched the vibe of the music. The music was intense and, well, I was as intense as you needed."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-43"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;43&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In both incarnations of the Rollins Band, Rollins combined spoken word with his traditional vocal style in songs such as "&lt;a href="/wiki/Liar_(Rollins_Band_song)" title="Liar (Rollins Band song)"&gt;Liar&lt;/a&gt;" (the song begins with a one-minute spoken diatribe by Rollins), as well as barking his way through songs (such as "Tearing" and "Starve") and employing the loud-quiet dynamic. &lt;i&gt;Rolling Stone&lt;/i&gt;'s Anthony DeCurtis names Rollins a "screeching hate machine" and his "hallmark" as "the sheets-of-sound assault".&lt;sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-44"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;44&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With the Rollins Band, his lyrics focused "almost exclusively on issues relating to personal integrity," according to critic Geoffrey Welchman.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-45"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;45&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="As_producer"&gt;As producer&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: As producer"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In the 1980s, Henry Rollins produced an album of acoustic songs for the famed convict &lt;a href="/wiki/Charles_Manson" title="Charles Manson"&gt;Charles Manson&lt;/a&gt; titled &lt;i&gt;Completion&lt;/i&gt;. The record was supposed to be released by &lt;a href="/wiki/SST_Records" title="SST Records"&gt;SST Records&lt;/a&gt;, but the project was later canceled due to the label receiving death threats for working with Manson. Only five test presses of &lt;i&gt;Completion&lt;/i&gt; were pressed, two of which remain in Rollins' possession.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-46"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;46&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 1995, Henry Rollins produced Australian hard rock band &lt;a href="/wiki/The_Mark_of_Cain_(band)" title="The Mark of Cain (band)"&gt;The Mark of Cain&lt;/a&gt;'s third full-length album &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Ill_at_Ease_(The_Mark_of_Cain_album)" title="Ill at Ease (The Mark of Cain album)"&gt;Ill at Ease&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-47"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;47&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Joe_Cole"&gt;Joe Cole&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Joe Cole"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins and his best friend &lt;a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole_(roadie)" title="Joe Cole (roadie)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Joe Cole&lt;/a&gt;, son of actor &lt;a href="/wiki/Dennis_Cole" title="Dennis Cole"&gt;Dennis Cole&lt;/a&gt;, were involved in a shooting when they were assaulted by robbers in December 1991 outside their shared Venice Beach, California home. Cole was killed after being shot in the face but Rollins escaped.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-LAT_48-0" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-LAT-48"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;48&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; The murder remains unsolved.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In an April 1992 &lt;a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times"&gt;Los Angeles Times&lt;/a&gt; interview (less than 6 months after Cole's death), Rollins revealed he kept a plastic container full of soil soaked with the blood of Joe Cole. Rollins said "I dug up all the earth where his head fellhe was shot in the faceand I've got all the dirt here, and so Joe Cole's in the house. I say good morning to him every day. I got his phone, too, so I got a direct line to him. So that feels good."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-LAT_48-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-LAT-48"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;48&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In a 2006 interview with Howard Stern, Rollins was asked if he had Joe Cole's brain in his house or had any of Joe Cole in his house. Rollins stated that the only thing he has of Joe Cole is memories. &lt;sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-49"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;49&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins has included Cole's story in his spoken word performances.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-50"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;50&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Media_work"&gt;Media work&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Media work"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Television"&gt;Television&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Television"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As Rollins rose to prominence with the Rollins Band, he began to present and appear on television. These included &lt;i&gt;Alternative Nation&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;MTV Sports&lt;/i&gt; in 1993 and 1994 respectively. Rollins also co starred in The Chase with Charlie Sheen. 1995 saw Rollins appear on an episode of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Unsolved_Mysteries" title="Unsolved Mysteries"&gt;Unsolved Mysteries&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; that explored the murder of his best friend &lt;a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole_(roadie)" title="Joe Cole (roadie)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Joe Cole&lt;/a&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-51"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;51&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and present &lt;i&gt;State of the Union Undressed&lt;/i&gt; on &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central"&gt;Comedy Central&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;. Rollins began to present and narrate &lt;i&gt;VH1 Legends&lt;/i&gt; in 1996.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-52"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;52&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins, busy with the Rollins Band, did not present more programs until 2001, but made appearances on a number of other television shows, including &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_Paradox" title="Welcome to Paradox"&gt;Welcome to Paradox&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; in 1998 in the episode "All Our Sins Forgotten", as a therapist who develops a device that can erase the bad memories of his patients. Rollins also voiced &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Mad_Stan" title="Mad Stan" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Mad Stan&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; in &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Batman_Beyond" title="Batman Beyond"&gt;Batman Beyond&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; in 1999 and 2000.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-53"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;53&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-54"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;54&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins was a host of film review programme &lt;i&gt;Henry's Film Corner&lt;/i&gt; on the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Independent_Film_Channel" title="Independent Film Channel" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Independent Film Channel&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, before presenting the weekly &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Henry_Rollins_Show" title="The Henry Rollins Show"&gt;The Henry Rollins Show&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; on the channel. The Henry Rollins Show is now being shown weekly on &lt;a href="/wiki/Film_24_(channel)" title="Film 24 (channel)"&gt;Film24&lt;/a&gt; along with Henry Rollins Uncut. The show also lead to a promotional tour in Europe that led to Henry being dubbed a bad boy goodwill ambassador by a NY reviewer.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-55"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;55&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;2002 saw Rollins guest star on an episode of the sitcom &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Drew_Carey_Show" title="The Drew Carey Show"&gt;The Drew Carey Show&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; as a man whom Oswald would find on &lt;a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay"&gt;eBay&lt;/a&gt; and pay to come to his house and "kick his ass". He co-hosted the British television show &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Full_Metal_Challenge" title="Full Metal Challenge"&gt;Full Metal Challenge&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, in which teams built vehicles to compete in various driving and racing contests, from 20022003 on &lt;a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4"&gt;Channel 4&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/TLC_(TV_channel)" title="TLC (TV channel)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;TLC&lt;/a&gt;. He has made a number of cameo appearances in television series such as MTV's &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Jackass_(TV_series)" title="Jackass (TV series)"&gt;Jackass&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and an episode of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Californication_(TV_series)" title="Californication (TV series)"&gt;Californication&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, where he played himself hosting a radio show.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-56"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;56&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2006, Rollins appeared in a documentary series by &lt;a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1"&gt;VH1&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Sundance_Channel_(United_States)" title="Sundance Channel (United States)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;The Sundance Channel&lt;/a&gt; called &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Drug_Years" title="The Drug Years"&gt;The Drug Years&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-57"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;57&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins appears in FX's &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Anarchy" title="Sons of Anarchy"&gt;Sons of Anarchy&lt;/a&gt;'s&lt;/i&gt; second season, which premiered in the fall of 2009 in the United States. Rollins plays A.J. Weston, a &lt;a href="/wiki/White-supremacist" title="White-supremacist" class="mw-redirect"&gt;white-supremacist&lt;/a&gt; gang leader and new antagonist in the show's fictional town of Charming, California, who poses a deadly threat to the Sons of Anarchy Motorcycle Club.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-58"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;58&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2009, Rollins voiced "Trucker" in &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!"&gt;American Dad!&lt;/a&gt;'s&lt;/i&gt; fourth season (episode eight).&lt;sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-59"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;59&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins voiced Benjamin Knox/Bonk in the &lt;a href="/wiki/2000_in_film" title="2000 in film"&gt;2000&lt;/a&gt; animated film &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Batman_Beyond:_Return_of_the_Joker" title="Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker"&gt;Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-60"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;60&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2010, Rollins appeared as a guest judge on Season 2 episode 6 of &lt;i&gt;RuPaul's Drag Race&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-61"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;61&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-62"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;62&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2011, he was interviewed in the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Explorer" title="National Geographic Explorer"&gt;National Geographic Explorer&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; episode "Born to Rage", regarding his possible link to the MAO gene (&lt;a href="/wiki/Warrior_gene" title="Warrior gene" class="mw-redirect"&gt;warrior gene&lt;/a&gt;) and violent behavior.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-63"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;63&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2012, he hosted the &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Wild" title="National Geographic Wild" class="mw-redirect"&gt;National Geographic Wild&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; series "Animal Underworld", investigating where the real boundaries lay in &lt;a href="/wiki/Human-animal_relationships" title="Human-animal relationships" class="mw-redirect"&gt;human-animal relationships&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-64"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;64&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In November 2013, Rollins started hosting the show &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/10_Things_You_Don%27t_Know_About" title="10 Things You Don't Know About"&gt;10 Things You Don't Know About&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; on the History Channel's &lt;a href="/wiki/H2_(TV_network)" title="H2 (TV network)"&gt;H2&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-65"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;65&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2014, he voiced the antagonist &lt;a href="/wiki/Zaheer_(The_Legend_of_Korra)" title="Zaheer (The Legend of Korra)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Zaheer&lt;/a&gt; in the &lt;a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Korra_(Book_3)" title="The Legend of Korra (Book 3)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;third season&lt;/a&gt; of the animated series &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Korra" title="The Legend of Korra"&gt;The Legend of Korra&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-66"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;66&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Radio"&gt;Radio&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Radio"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;On May 19, 2004, Rollins began hosting a weekly radio show, &lt;i&gt;Harmony in My Head&lt;/i&gt;, on &lt;a href="/wiki/Indie_103.1" title="Indie 103.1"&gt;Indie 103.1&lt;/a&gt; radio in Los Angeles. The show aired every Monday evening, with Rollins playing music ranging from early rock and &lt;a href="/wiki/Jump_blues" title="Jump blues"&gt;jump blues&lt;/a&gt; to &lt;a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock"&gt;hard rock&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Blues_rock" title="Blues rock"&gt;blues rock&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Folk_rock" title="Folk rock"&gt;folk rock&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock"&gt;punk rock&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music"&gt;heavy metal&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Rockabilly" title="Rockabilly"&gt;rockabilly&lt;/a&gt;, and touching on &lt;a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music"&gt;hip hop&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz"&gt;jazz&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music"&gt;world music&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae"&gt;reggae&lt;/a&gt;, classical music and more. &lt;i&gt;Harmony in my Head&lt;/i&gt; often emphasizes B-sides, live &lt;a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording"&gt;bootlegs&lt;/a&gt; and other rarities, and nearly every episode has featured a song either by the &lt;a href="/wiki/Beastie_Boys" title="Beastie Boys"&gt;Beastie Boys&lt;/a&gt; or British group &lt;a href="/wiki/The_Fall_(band)" title="The Fall (band)"&gt;The Fall&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins put the show on a short hiatus to undertake a spoken-word tour in early 2005. Rollins posted playlists and commentary on-line; these lists were expanded with more information and published in book form as &lt;i&gt;Fanatic!&lt;/i&gt; through 2.13.61 in November 2005. In late 2005, Rollins announced the show's return and began the first episode by playing the show's namesake &lt;a href="/wiki/Buzzcocks" title="Buzzcocks"&gt;Buzzcocks&lt;/a&gt; song. As of 2008, the show continues each week despite Rollins's constant touring with new pre-recorded shows between live broadcasts. In 2009 Indie 103.1 went off the air, although it continues to broadcast over the Internet.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2007, Rollins published &lt;i&gt;Fanatic! Vol. 2&lt;/i&gt; through 2.13.61. &lt;i&gt;Fanatic! Vol. 3&lt;/i&gt; was released in the fall of 2008. On February 18, 2009, &lt;a href="/wiki/KCRW" title="KCRW"&gt;KCRW&lt;/a&gt; announced that Rollins would be hosting a live show on Saturday nights starting March 7, 2009.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-67"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;67&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2011 Rollins was interviewed on Episode 121 of American Public Media's podcast, "The Dinner Party Download", posted on November 3, 2011.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Film"&gt;Film&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Film"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins began his film career appearing in several independent films featuring the band Black Flag. His film debut was in 1982's &lt;i&gt;The Slog Movie&lt;/i&gt;, about the West Coast punk scene.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-68"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;68&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; An appearance in 1985's &lt;i&gt;Black Flag Live&lt;/i&gt; followed. Rollins' first film appearance without Black Flag was the short film &lt;i&gt;The Right Side of My Brain&lt;/i&gt; with &lt;a href="/wiki/Lydia_Lunch" title="Lydia Lunch"&gt;Lydia Lunch&lt;/a&gt; in 1985.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-69"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;69&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Following the band's breakup, Rollins did not appear in any films until 1994's &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Chase_(1994_film)" title="The Chase (1994 film)"&gt;The Chase&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;. Rollins appeared in the 2007 direct-to-DVD sequel to &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Wrong_Turn" title="Wrong Turn"&gt;Wrong Turn&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2003), &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Wrong_Turn_2:_Dead_End" title="Wrong Turn 2: Dead End"&gt;Wrong Turn 2: Dead End&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; as a retired Marine Corps officer who hosts his own show which tests the contestants' will to survive. Rollins has also appeared in &lt;i&gt;Punk: Attitude&lt;/i&gt;, a documentary on the punk scene, and in &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/American_Hardcore_(film)" title="American Hardcore (film)"&gt;American Hardcore&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2006). In 2012, Henry Rollins appeared in a short documentary entitled "Who Shot Rock and Roll" discussing the early punk scene in Los Angeles as well as photographs of himself in Black Flag taken by esteemed photographer Edward Colver.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-70"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;70&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Some feature-length movies Henry Rollins has appeared in include:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;Kiss Napoleon Goodbye&lt;/i&gt; (1990), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Lydia_Lunch" title="Lydia Lunch"&gt;Lydia Lunch&lt;/a&gt; and Don Bajema&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Chase_(1994_film)" title="The Chase (1994 film)"&gt;The Chase&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (1994), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Charlie_Sheen" title="Charlie Sheen"&gt;Charlie Sheen&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Johnny_Mnemonic_(film)" title="Johnny Mnemonic (film)"&gt;Johnny Mnemonic&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (1995), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Keanu_Reeves" title="Keanu Reeves"&gt;Keanu Reeves&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Ice-T" title="Ice-T"&gt;Ice-T&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Dolph_Lundgren" title="Dolph Lundgren"&gt;Dolph Lundgren&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Heat_(1995_film)" title="Heat (1995 film)"&gt;Heat&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (1995), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Al_Pacino" title="Al Pacino"&gt;Al Pacino&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro"&gt;Robert De Niro&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Val_Kilmer" title="Val Kilmer"&gt;Val Kilmer&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Lost_Highway_(film)" title="Lost Highway (film)"&gt;Lost Highway&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (1997), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Bill_Pullman" title="Bill Pullman"&gt;Bill Pullman&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Patricia_Arquette" title="Patricia Arquette"&gt;Patricia Arquette&lt;/a&gt;; directed by &lt;a href="/wiki/David_Lynch" title="David Lynch"&gt;David Lynch&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Jack_Frost_(1998_film)" title="Jack Frost (1998 film)"&gt;Jack Frost&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (1998), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Michael_Keaton" title="Michael Keaton"&gt;Michael Keaton&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Batman_Beyond:_Return_of_the_Joker" title="Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker"&gt;Batman Beyond: Return of the Joker&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2000), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Kevin_Conroy" title="Kevin Conroy"&gt;Kevin Conroy&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Mark_Hamill" title="Mark Hamill"&gt;Mark Hamill&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Morgan%27s_Ferry" title="Morgan's Ferry"&gt;Morgan's Ferry&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2001), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Billy_Zane" title="Billy Zane"&gt;Billy Zane&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Kelly_McGillis" title="Kelly McGillis"&gt;Kelly McGillis&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Dogtown_and_Z-Boys" title="Dogtown and Z-Boys"&gt;Dogtown and Z-Boys&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2001 documentary)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Scenes_of_the_Crime" title="Scenes of the Crime"&gt;Scenes of the Crime&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2001), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bridges" title="Jeff Bridges"&gt;Jeff Bridges&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_New_Guy" title="The New Guy"&gt;The New Guy&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2002), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lee" title="Tommy Lee"&gt;Tommy Lee&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/DJ_Qualls" title="DJ Qualls"&gt;DJ Qualls&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Jackass_The_Movie" title="Jackass The Movie" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Jackass The Movie&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2002) with &lt;a href="/wiki/Johnny_Knoxville" title="Johnny Knoxville"&gt;Johnny Knoxville&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Bam_Margera" title="Bam Margera"&gt;Bam Margera&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Bad_Boys_II" title="Bad Boys II"&gt;Bad Boys II&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2003) with &lt;a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith"&gt;Will Smith&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Martin_Lawrence" title="Martin Lawrence"&gt;Martin Lawrence&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;Deathdealer: A Documentary&lt;/i&gt; (2004)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Feast_(2005_film)" title="Feast (2005 film)"&gt;Feast&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2005), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Balthazar_Getty" title="Balthazar Getty"&gt;Balthazar Getty&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Navi_Rawat" title="Navi Rawat"&gt;Navi Rawat&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Jackass_Number_Two" title="Jackass Number Two"&gt;Jackass Number Two&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2006), with &lt;a href="/wiki/Preston_Lacy" title="Preston Lacy"&gt;Preston Lacy&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="/wiki/Steve-O" title="Steve-O"&gt;Steve-O&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Chris_Pontius" title="Chris Pontius"&gt;Chris Pontius&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Alibi" title="The Alibi"&gt;The Alibi&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2006)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Wrong_Turn_2:_Dead_End" title="Wrong Turn 2: Dead End"&gt;Wrong Turn 2: Dead End&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2007)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Devil%27s_Tomb" title="The Devil's Tomb"&gt;The Devil's Tomb&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2009)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;H for Hunger&lt;/i&gt; (2009 documentary)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/William_Shatner%27s_Gonzo_Ballet" title="William Shatner's Gonzo Ballet"&gt;William Shatner's Gonzo Ballet&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2009 documentary)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/DC_Universe_Animated_Original_Movies#Green_Lantern:_Emerald_Knights" title="DC Universe Animated Original Movies"&gt;Green Lantern: Emerald Knights&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2011) as Kilowog&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/West_of_Memphis" title="West of Memphis"&gt;West of Memphis&lt;/a&gt; (2012 documentary)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Downloaded_(film)" title="Downloaded (film)"&gt;Downloaded&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2013 documentary)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/He_Never_Died" title="He Never Died"&gt;He Never Died&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (2015), With &lt;a href="/wiki/Steven_Ogg" title="Steven Ogg"&gt;Steven Ogg&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="/wiki/Booboo_Stewart" title="Booboo Stewart"&gt;Booboo Stewart&lt;/a&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-71"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;71&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Books_and_audiobooks"&gt;Books and audiobooks&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Books and audiobooks"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins has written a variety of books, including &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Black_Coffee_Blues" title="Black Coffee Blues"&gt;Black Coffee Blues&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Do I Come Here Often?&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;The First Five&lt;/i&gt; (a compilation of &lt;i&gt;High Adventure in the Great Outdoors&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Pissing in the Gene Pool&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Bang!&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Art to Choke Hearts&lt;/i&gt;, and &lt;i&gt;One From None&lt;/i&gt;), &lt;i&gt;See a Grown Man Cry&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Now Watch Him Die&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Smile,_You%27re_Traveling" title="Smile, You're Traveling"&gt;Smile, You're Traveling&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Get_in_the_Van" title="Get in the Van"&gt;Get in the Van&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Everything_(book)" title="Everything (book)" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Eye Scream&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Broken Summers&lt;/i&gt;, &lt;i&gt;Roomanitarian&lt;/i&gt;, and &lt;i&gt;Solipsist&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For the &lt;a href="/wiki/Audiobook" title="Audiobook"&gt;audiobook&lt;/a&gt; version of the 2006 novel &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/World_War_Z" title="World War Z"&gt;World War Z&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; Rollins voiced the character of T. Sean Collins, a mercenary hired to protect celebrities during a mass panic caused by an onslaught of the undead. Rollins' other audiobook recordings include &lt;i&gt;3:10 to Yuma&lt;/i&gt; and his own autobiographical book &lt;i&gt;Get in the Van&lt;/i&gt;, for which he won a &lt;a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Grammy Award&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Online_journalism"&gt;Online journalism&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Online journalism"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In September 2008, Rollins began contributing to the "Politics &amp; Power" &lt;a href="/wiki/Weblog" title="Weblog" class="mw-redirect"&gt;blog&lt;/a&gt; at the online version of &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)"&gt;Vanity Fair&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; magazine.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-72"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;72&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Since March 2009, his posts have appeared under their own sub-title, &lt;i&gt;Straight Talk Espresso&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-73"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;73&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; His posts consistently direct harsh criticism at &lt;a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States"&gt;conservative&lt;/a&gt; politicians and pundits, although he does occasionally target those on the left.&lt;sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;[&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"&gt;&lt;span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)"&gt;citation needed&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;]&lt;/sup&gt; In August 2010, he began writing a music column for &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly"&gt;LA Weekly&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; in Los Angeles.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-laweekly_1-1" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-laweekly-1"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;1&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; In 2012, Rollins began publishing articles with &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" title="The Huffington Post"&gt;The Huffington Post&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and alternative news website &lt;i&gt;WordswithMeaning!&lt;/i&gt;. In the months leading up to the &lt;a href="/wiki/2012_United_States_Presidential_election" title="2012 United States Presidential election" class="mw-redirect"&gt;2012 United States Presidential election&lt;/a&gt;, Rollins broadcast a YouTube series called "Capitalism 2012", in which he toured the capital cities of the US states, interviewing people about current issues.&lt;sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;[&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"&gt;&lt;span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)"&gt;citation needed&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;]&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Spoken_word"&gt;Spoken word&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Spoken word"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins also has toured all over the world doing spoken word performances and his shows frequently last for over three hours. His spoken word style encompasses stand up comedy, accounts of experiences he's had in the world of music and during his extensive travels around the globe, self-deprecating stories about his own shortcomings, introspective recollections from his own life (such as the death of his friend, Joe Cole), intense commentaries on society and playful, sometimes vulgar, anecdotes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games"&gt;Video games&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Video games"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins was a playable character in both &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Def_Jam:_Fight_for_NY" title="Def Jam: Fight for NY"&gt;Def Jam: Fight for NY&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Fight_for_NY:_The_Takeover" title="Def Jam Fight for NY: The Takeover"&gt;Def Jam Fight for NY: The Takeover&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;. Rollins is also the voice of Mace Griffin in &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Mace_Griffin:_Bounty_Hunter" title="Mace Griffin: Bounty Hunter"&gt;Mace Griffin: Bounty Hunter&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Campaigning_and_activism"&gt;Campaigning and activism&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Campaigning and activism"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;div class="thumb tright"&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg" class="image"&gt;&lt;img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg/220px-Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg/330px-Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg/440px-Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="924" data-file-height="653" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;div class="thumbcaption"&gt;
&lt;div class="magnify"&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Rollins_in_Iraq_with_USO_tour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
Rollins signing an autograph while on a &lt;a href="/wiki/United_Service_Organizations" title="United Service Organizations"&gt;United Service Organizations&lt;/a&gt; (USO) tour in &lt;a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq"&gt;Iraq&lt;/a&gt; in 2003.&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rollins has become an outspoken human rights activist, most vocally for &lt;a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country" title="LGBT rights by country" class="mw-redirect"&gt;gay rights&lt;/a&gt;. Rollins frequently speaks out on social justice on his spoken word tours and promotes equality, regardless of sexuality.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-74"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;74&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He was the host of the WedRock &lt;a href="/wiki/Benefit_concert" title="Benefit concert"&gt;benefit concert&lt;/a&gt;, which raised money for a pro-gay-marriage organization.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;During the &lt;a href="/wiki/2003_Iraq_War" title="2003 Iraq War" class="mw-redirect"&gt;2003 Iraq War&lt;/a&gt;, he started touring with the &lt;a href="/wiki/United_Service_Organizations" title="United Service Organizations"&gt;United Service Organizations&lt;/a&gt; to entertain troops overseas while remaining against the war, leading him to once cause a stir at a base in &lt;a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan"&gt;Kyrgyzstan&lt;/a&gt; when he told the crowd: "Your commander would never lie to you. That's the vice president's job."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-75"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;75&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins believes it is important that he performs to the troops so that they have multiple points of contact with the rest of the world, stating that "they can get really cut loose from planet earth."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-76"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;76&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; He has made eight tours, including visits to bases in Djibouti, Kuwait, Iraq, Kyrgyzstan, Afghanistan (twice), Egypt, Turkey, Qatar, Honduras, Japan, Korea and the United Arab Emirates.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-77"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;77&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He has also been active in the campaign to free the "&lt;a href="/wiki/West_Memphis_3" title="West Memphis 3" class="mw-redirect"&gt;West Memphis Three&lt;/a&gt;"three young men who were believed by their supporters to have been wrongfully convicted of murder, and who have since been released from prison, but not exonerated. Rollins appears with &lt;a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)" title="Public Enemy (band)"&gt;Public Enemy&lt;/a&gt; frontman &lt;a href="/wiki/Chuck_D" title="Chuck D"&gt;Chuck D&lt;/a&gt; on the &lt;a href="/wiki/Black_Flag_(band)" title="Black Flag (band)"&gt;Black Flag&lt;/a&gt; song "Rise Above" on the benefit album &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Rise_Above:_24_Black_Flag_Songs_to_Benefit_the_West_Memphis_Three" title="Rise Above: 24 Black Flag Songs to Benefit the West Memphis Three"&gt;Rise Above: 24 Black Flag Songs to Benefit the West Memphis Three&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;, the first time Rollins had performed Black Flag's material since 1986.&lt;sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-78"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;78&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Continuing his activism on behalf of US troops and veterans, Rollins joined &lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Iraq_and_Afghanistan_Veterans_of_America" title="Iraq and Afghanistan Veterans of America"&gt;Iraq and Afghanistan Veterans of America&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt; (IAVA) in 2008 to launch a public service advertisement campaign, CommunityofVeterans.org, which helps veterans coming home from war reintegrate into their communities. In April 2009, Rollins helped IAVA launch the second phase of the campaign which engages the friends and family of Iraq and Afghanistan veterans at SupportYourVet.org.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;On December 3, 2009, Rollins wrote of his support for the victims of the &lt;a href="/wiki/Bhopal_disaster" title="Bhopal disaster"&gt;Bhopal disaster&lt;/a&gt; in India, in an article for &lt;a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)"&gt;Vanity Fair&lt;/a&gt;&lt;sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-79"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;79&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; 25 yearsto the dayafter the &lt;a href="/wiki/Methyl_isocyanate" title="Methyl isocyanate"&gt;methyl isocyanate&lt;/a&gt; gas leak from the &lt;a href="/wiki/Union_Carbide_Corporation" title="Union Carbide Corporation" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Union Carbide Corporation&lt;/a&gt;'s pesticide factory exposed more than half a million local people to poisonous gas and resulted in the death of 17,000. He spent time in Bhopal with the people, to listen to their stories. In a later radio interview in February 2010&lt;sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-80"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;80&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; Rollins summed up his approach to activism, "This is where my anger takes me, to places like this, not into abuse but into proactive, clean movement."&lt;sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"&gt;&lt;a href="#cite_note-81"&gt;&lt;span&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;81&lt;span&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Works"&gt;Works&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Works"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle"&gt;Main article: &lt;a href="/wiki/Works_of_Henry_Rollins" title="Works of Henry Rollins" class="mw-redirect"&gt;Works of Henry Rollins&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_releases"&gt;Musical releases&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Musical releases"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;

&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="/wiki/Who%27s_Got_the_10%C2%BD%3F" title="Who's Got the 10?"&gt;Who's Got the 10?&lt;/a&gt; (1986)&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/li&gt;

&lt;h4&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="As_Henry_Rollins"&gt;As Henry Rollins&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: As Henry Rollins"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;

&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;&lt;span class="mw-headline" id="With_Wartime"&gt;With Wartime&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection"&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;[&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry_Rollins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: With Wartime"&gt;edit&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class="mw-editsection-bracket"&gt;]&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fast Food For Thought&lt;/i&gt; (1990)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
